+Jamison Brereton

61
Indra
Nodhas Gautama
16 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The three Indra hymns by Nodhas share a ritual context: judging from their last verses (I.61.16, 62.13, 63.9) they were all composed to accompany the H─Бriyojana (тАЬFallow-bay-yokingтАЭ) oblation, when IndraтАЩs pair of horses is yoked up for the godтАЩs return journey to heaven after the sacrifice is complete. The parts of these hymns before the final verse do not seem to reflect this ritual moment, and the three hymns are quite different, though they all display NodhasтАЩs remarkable poetic skill.
This first hymn, I.61, is a masterpiece of intricate structure and verbal trickery. We will summarize the main points here, but for more detailed treatment see the lengthy discussion in Jamison (2007: 60тАУ68). The most obvious structural device is the fronted repetition of a deictic pronoun: each of the sixteen verses except the last (which is an extra-hymnic summary verse) begins with either the dative asma├н тАЬfor himтАЭ or the genitive asy├б тАЬof him,тАЭ followed by two emphasizing particles, always referring to Indra (except in vs. 12тАФsee below). The dative sequence is the more common and frames the hymn (vss. 1тАУ6, 8, 12, 15); the genitive sequence is found primarily in the center of the hymn (vss. 7, 9тАУ11, 13тАУ14).
This rigid structural device both parallels and counterpoints the semantic structure of the hymn. In general in this hymn the dative verses express the ritual here-and-now, with the production and presentation of hymns and ritual offer ings тАЬto/for just this one,тАЭ while the genitive verses concern IndraтАЩs great deeds. Especially in the dative verses numerous co-referential adjectival datives reinforce the fronted pronoun, as well as strategically placed dative tokens of the godтАЩs name. Curiously, in the genitive verses the genitive several times (vss. 7, 10, 11) seems to have quite a loose syntactic connection to the rest of the sentence, and Indra may appear in another case in the same verse, as in

> 61.10ab asy├йd ev├б ┼Ы├бvas─Б ┼Ыuс╣г├бntaс╣Г, v├н vr╠е┼Ыcad v├бjreс╣Зa vr╠еtr├бm ├нndraс╕е
> Of just this one [gen.]тАФin (his) expansion Indra [nom.] hewed apart snorting Vr╠еtra with his mace.

But what may appear superficially to be clumsy composition serves a larger structural purpose: it seems that the logical structure of the hymn requires a two-way opposition, between dative asma├н and something else: the something else is genitive asy├б even when a different case form might have been more appropriate, for a variety of other cases would have obscured the bipartite contrastive structure of the hymn. Here we see an example of clausal morphosyntax subordinated to and indeed distorted by the imposition of a larger literary and rhetorical pattern.
The poet Nodhas also lays a few traps for us by playing on the expectations he has created. Most notable of them is verse 12, which begins with the dative asma├н and therefore appears to return us from the mythological past to the realm of the current-day poet of verses 1тАУ5, an expectation reinforced by the verb pr├б bhar─Б, a standard lexeme for presenting a hymn to a divinity. But the phrase in verse 12 quickly goes awry. At the opening of the next p─Бda, where IndraтАЩs name has been prominently placed in previous verses (├нndr─Бya 1d, 4d, 5b, 8b), we find, most shock ingly, the name of his arch-enemy, vr╠еtr─Б╠Бya, immediately followed by the accusative object v├бjram, IndraтАЩs weapon, not the word for hymn we were expecting. The poet has simply tricked us, having laid a trap with conventional phraseology and syntax and with the stylistic patterns established earlier in the hymn. He also skillfully exploits the morphological ambiguity of the verb form bhar─Б: given the pattern set in verses 1тАУ5 we are primed to interpret bhar─Б as a 1st sg. subjunctive (тАЬI shall pres
entтАЭ), but as the half verse unfolds, it becomes clear that bhar─Б must rather be taken as a metrically lengthened 2nd singular imperative (тАЬbear down!тАЭ).
The meter of this hymn is often irregular, with a number of ten-syllable lines, but again this irregularity should not be taken as a sign of poor poetic technique. Rather the hymn seems to be phrase-driven rather than meter-driven, and the metri cal rests that result from тАЬmissing syllablesтАЭ serve to isolate and emphasize crucial nominal phrasesтАФan effect also heightened by the copious examples of alliteration.
With all the poetic fireworks on display the actual contents of the hymn may seem almost beside the point, but we will provide a brief sketch. The first five verses (тАЬdative versesтАЭ) are variations on a theme: the poetтАЩs verbal offerings to Indra. The sixth verse, also a dative verse, modulates to the distant past and the god Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs gift of the newly fashioned mace to Indra. Verse 7 combines two rare Indra myths: his appropriation of his fatherтАЩs soma right after his birth and the Emuс╣гa myth, in which the god Viс╣гс╣Зu steals a mess of rice porridge while Indra shoots the boar Emuс╣гa. (For further on this myth, see Introduction, p. 40.) Verses 8тАУ12 treat the Vr╠еtra myth for the most part, though with some detours. Verses 13тАУ15 generalize the praise of IndraтАЩs deeds and bring it back to the present time and to the present poet, Nodhas, who names himself in verse 14, while the final verse, 16, summarizes the hymn that precedes and names the ritual application, the тАЬFallow-bay-yokingтАЭ oblation.
It is difficult to do justice to this tour de force of poetic craft, and many of its finest effects have not been discussed here. It is, unfortunately, even more difficult to do justice to it in English translation.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI offer adoration to that powerful, rapid, mighty, praise-meriting, and unobstructed Indra; adoration that is acceptable, and oblations that are grateful, as food (to a hungry man).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Just for this one, powerful, precipitous, mighty, do I bring forward praise like a pleasurable offeringтАФ
for the one equal to song, not poor, (do I bring) a laudтАФfor Indra (I bring) sacred formulations best bestowed.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

с╣Ы╠Бc─лс╣гama-, an epithet of Indra, is an impossible word; Geldner wisely refuses to tr. it.

However, it is difficult not to see in it a combination of с╣Ы╠Бc- тАШchant, songтАЩ and sam├б- тАШlike, sameтАЩ, however obscure the morphological details are - and obscure they certainly are. The first member cannot, straightforwardly, be a case form of с╣Ы╠Бcbecause the case-ending should be accented. The length of the -─л- might be analogical to the long ─л in phonologically similar с╣Ыj─лp├нn-, с╣Ыj─лс╣г├нn-, but motivating a short -i- (in putative *с╣Ы╠Бci-) is hard enough (Caland compounding form, like ┼Ы├║ci-?). It is tempting (and some have succumbed to the temptation) to connect -sama- with another designation of ritual speech, s─Б╠Бman-, but the difference in vowel length is probably fatal. Note that in our passage the word is adjacent to another old crux, ├бdhrigu-, the controversies about which (see KEWA and EWA s.v.) should have been definitely settled by comparison with OAv. drigu- тАШpoor, needyтАЩ (Narten, YH 238-40). Both с╣Ы╠Бc─лс╣гama- and ├бdrigu- are disproportionately represented in the VIIIth Maс╣Зс╕Нala, the home of much aberrant vocabulary. In the end those who elect to tr. с╣Ы╠Бc─лс╣гama- take it as a compound of the two elements suggested above: Renou тАШ├йgal ├а la stropheтАЩ, Witzel Got┼Н (somewhat peculiarly, though starting with the same elements) тАШder im Preislied (immer) als dieselbe Person erscheint (?)тАЩ; so also the published translation тАШequal to songтАЩ. For further, see EWA s.v. ### 01-02 Here and throughout the hymn, there is a certain amount of phonological and lexical chaining (in addition to the repeated fronted demonstratives). Here 2b bh├бr─Бmi picks up both 1c harmi and 1d br├бhm─Бс╣Зi, and 2a asm─Б╠Б├нd u pr├бyaс╕е тАж pr├б yaс╣Гsi playfully echoes 1a asm─Б╠Б├нd u pr├бтАж, with pr├бyaс╕е of 1b substituted for the bare preverb pr├б.

+Griffith

EVEN to him, swift, strong and high. exalted, I bring my song of praise as dainty viands,
My thought to him resistless, praise-deserving, prayers offered most especially to Indra.

+Geldner

Ihm, dem Starken, ├Ьberlegenen, bringe ich das Loblied wie Labsal dar, dem M├дchtigen, dem …….., nicht Kargen ein Lobeswort, dem Indra erbauliche Reden als bestes Geschenk.

+Grassmann

Ihm bring’ ich nun dem m├дchtigen, dem schnellen, wie Labetrunk das Loblied dar, dem grossen, Dem lichten Indra, der unhemmbar schreitet, geweihteste Gebete ihm als Gabe.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI offer (oblations, acceptable as) food (to the hungry), to that Indra; I raise (to him) exclamations that may be of efficacy in discomfiting (my foe); others (also) worship Indra, the ancient lord, in heart, in mind, and in understanding.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Just to this one I have held it out like a pleasurable offering. I bring out a song; I thrust it out with a good twist
to Indra, with heart, with mind, with inspired thought. For the
primordial lord the insights groom themselves.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In addition to the inter-verse echoes just noted, alliteration in 2c m├бnas─Б man─лс╣г─Б╠Бand 2d pratn─Б╠Бya p├бtye. Jesse Lundquist adds 2a pr├бya iva pr├б yaс╣Гsi.

b─Б╠Бdhe in 2b is universally taken as a dat. infinitive (as it is in I.132.5), but this makes semantic difficulties because тИЪb─Бdh means тАШthrust, press, oppressтАЩ. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬum (ihn) тАж zu n├╢tigen(?),тАЭ RenouтАЩs тАЬpour contraindre (le dieu),тАЭ and Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬum (ihn) тАж zu ├╝berh├дufenтАЭ thus misrepresent the sense of the verb. The тИЪb─Бdh is esp. common with the preverbs ├бpa and v├н in the meanings тАШthrust away, thrust apartтАЩ, but I here take the pr├б of p─Бda a with both verbs (bh├бr─Бmi and b─Б╠Бdhe) in p─Бda b. As for morphology, I take b─Б╠Бdhe as a 1st sg. mid. pres. (the root is always inflected in the middle), rather than as an infinitive, which allows the root to maintain its standard sense: I push the hymn toward Indra with particular forcefulness. As a finite verb, b─Б╠Бdhe owes its accent to its initial position in the new clause.

suvс╣Ыkt├н- is a bahuvr─лhi specialized for praise hymns (and occasionally the gods who receive them) and is often simply tr. тАШpraise(-song)тАЩ (e.g., Geldner тАШPreisтАЩ here). I prefer to render it literally; -vс╣Ыkt├н- belongs to the root тИЪvс╣Ыj тАШtwistтАЩ, and the English idiom тАЬgood twistтАЭ refers to particularly clever turns in a plot or other verbal products.

Most tr. take c with d, not ab. This is possible, but not necessary.

+Griffith

Praise, like oblation, I present, and utter aloud my song, my fair hymn to the Victor.
For Indra, who is Lord of old, the singers have decked their lauds with heart and mind and spirit.

+Geldner

Ihm Biete ich ein Loblied wie ein Labsal an und bringe es dar, um ihn mit Preis zu n├╢tigen. F├╝r Indra als Ihren alten Gemahl putzen sie die Gedicht mit Herz, Denken und Sinnen aus.

+Grassmann

Wie Labetrunk reich’ ich ihm dar und bring’ ihm den Lobgesang, mit Liedern ihn best├╝rmend; dem alten Herrscher Indra soll man schm├╝cken mit Herz und Geist und weisem Sinn Gebete.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI offer with my mouth a loud acclamation, with powerful and pure words of praise, to exalt him who is the type (of all), the giver (of good things), the great, the wise.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Just to this one this utmost sun-winning song do I bring with
my mouth,
to strengthen the most munificent patron with the invitations of my thoughts, with their good twists.

+Griffith

To him then with my lips mine adoration, winning heaven’s light, most excellent, I offer,
To magnify with songs of invocation and with fair hymns the Lord, most bounteous Giver.

+Geldner

Ihm bringe ich mit dem Munde dieses h├╢chste sonnengewinnende Loblied dar, um den freigebigsten Herren zu erheben mit den Einladungen und Lobpreisungen der Gedichte.

+Grassmann

Ihm bring’ ich mit dem Munde diesen h├╢chsten, des Himmels Gl├╝ck verschaffenden Gesang dar, Um mit des Geist’s Begr├╝ssungen und Liedern den gabenreichsten F├╝rsten zu erheben.

рдЗрддрд┐ рдорддреНрд╡рд░реНрдереАрдп рдЗрд░рдиреН ред рдирд┐рддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╛рджреНрдпреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡рдореН рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI prepare praises fo rhim, as a carpenter constructs a car, (that the driver) may thence (obtain) food; praises well deserved, to him who is entitled to commendation, and excellent oblations to the wise Indra.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ratham na taс╣гс╣нeva tatsin─Бya: sina = food;

Tat = owner of the car, i.e. for his food

+Jamison Brereton

Just for this one I put together praiseтАФlike a carpenter a chariot for the one whose gear it isтАФ
and hymns with a good twist for the one whose vehicle is hymnsтАФfor wise Indra (praise) that sets everything in motion.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner suggests (in n. 3 to his n. to 4ab), the apparent pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ doubling of the simile particle (r├бthaс╣Г n├б t─Б╠Бс╣гс╣н─Б-iva) may instead signal that two images have been crossed here: one with a simplex hinomi (тАЬI impel the praise like a chariotтАЭ) and the other with s├бс╣Г hinomi and the addition of the carpenter as subject (тАЬI, like a carpenter, put together praise, like a chariotтАЭ).

+Griffith

Even for him I frame a laud, as fashions the wright a chariot for the man who needs it,–
Praises to him who gladly hears our praises, a hymn well-formed, all-moving, to wise Indra.

+Geldner

Ihm f├╝ge ich den Preisgesang zusammen wie der Zimmermann den Wagen f├╝r ihn, der Lohn daf├╝r bezahlt, ihn belohnt, und Lobreden f├╝r ihn, den die Lobreden anziehen, zum Preis f├╝r den verst├дndnisvollen Indra den allbewegenden Preisgesang.

+Grassmann

Ihm r├╝st’ ich zu mein Loblied wie den Wagen der Wagenbauer dem, der ihn begehret; Dem Liederfreunde Lieder, sch├╢n bereitend, dem weisen Indra Lob, das durch die Welt dringt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬTo propitiate that Indra for the sake of food, I combinepraise with utterance, as (a man harnesses) a horse (to a car), in order to celebrate the heroic, munificent, and food-conferring Indra, the destroyer of the cities (of the asuras).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Juhv─Б: the instrumental ument of invocation, the organ of speech;

Arkam: hymnb or praise in metre

+Jamison Brereton

Just for this one, for Indra, do I anoint the chant with my tongue [/the offering ladle], as one anoints a team when seeking fameтАФ
to extol the hero accustomed to giving [/gifts], the splitter of
strongholds whose fame is sung.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

juhv─Б╠Аhas its standard double meaning, тАШtongueтАЩ and тАШoffering ladleтАЩ, a pun that is enabled by the verb s├бm a├▒je тАЬI anointтАЭ: anointing with the tongue means producing praise, while тАШoffering ladleтАЩ fits better with the literal meaning of the verb.

d─Бna├║kas- is likewise of double sense, both тАШaccustomed to givingтАЩ and тАШaccustomed to giftsтАЩ, representing the reciprocal trade in praise and sacrifice given to the gods, in return for the godsтАЩ material gifts to us.

+Griffith

So with my tongue I deck, to please that Indra, my hymn, as ’twere a horse, through love of glory,
To reverence the Hero, bounteous Giver, famed far and wide, destroyer of the castles.

+Geldner

F├╝r ihn will ich, wie man ein Rennpferd salbt, um Ruhm zu gewinnen, f├╝r Indra das Preislied mit der Zunge salbungsvoll machen, um den schenkgewohnten Helden zu loben, den Brecher der Burgen, dessen Ruhm gefeiert wird.

+Grassmann

Ihm schm├╝cke ich voll Schatzbegier das Preislied, mit meiner Zung’ dem Indra wie ein Ross aus; Den Mann zu preisen, der am Opfer Lust hat, den Burgzerst├╢rer, dessen Ruhm man preiset.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬFor that Indra, verily Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б sharpened the well-acting, sure-aimed thunderbolt for the battle, with which fatal (weapon) the foe-subduing and mighty sovereign severed the limbs of Vс╣Ыtra.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Just for this one Tvaс╣гс╣нar fashioned the mace of best workmanship, the reverberating one, for battle [/for joy],
with which he found the mortal spot of that very Vr╠еtra, as, gaining mastery, he thrust with the thrusting (mace), while conferring (who knows) how much.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The tv├бс╣гс╣н─Б here has been prepared for by 4b t├бс╣гс╣н─Б, and both appear in alliterative phrases: t├бс╣гс╣нeva t├бtsin─Бya and tv├бс╣гс╣н─Б takс╣гat.

Another word with a standard double sense: r├бс╣Зa-; both senses are possible here, also in vs. 9 below.

The position of y├йna in this subordinate clause is anomalous, as we expect at most one constituent to precede the y├б- form. I have no explanation, but there is much that is off-kilter in the deployment of sentence parts in this hymn.

IтАЩve tr. the participle tuj├бn as it were a finite verb, because the English otherwise dribbles off into unintelligibility. In fact, because of the rel. cl. in c, itтАЩs better to take d as a new cl. with tuj├бn as predicated participle (тАЬGaining mastery, he was thrusting тАжтАЭ). On this stem see comm. ad IX.91.4.

The unclear kiyedh─Б╠Б- is found only here and in vs. 12. See EWA s.v. and ScarlattaтАЩs (250-52) discussions of previous attempts at explanation. I favor the suggestion registered (and dismissed) by Scarlatta that it consists of the weak stem of k├нyant-тАШhow much, how greatтАЩ + the root noun dh─Б╠Б-, with the development *-nt╠е-dh- >

*-adzdh- > *-azdh- > -edh-, despite HoffmannтАЩs dismissal of the posited phonological development (Aufs. 400)тАФalthough I recognize the phonological problems of this solution. RenouтАЩs тАЬlui qui conf├иre (on ne sait) combienтАЭ represents this etymology one way or the other.

+Griffith

Even for him hath Tvastar forged the thunder, most deftly wrought, celestial, for the battle,
Wherewith he reached the vital parts of Vrtra, striking-the vast, the mighty with the striker.

+Geldner

Ihm zimmerte Tvastri die Keule, die sehr kunstreiche, sausende zum Kampfe, mit der er sogar des Vritra verwundbare Stelle fand, als er mit der losfahrenden Keule auf ihn losfuhr, allverm├╢gend, was es auch sei schaffend.

+Grassmann

Ihm hat zur Schlacht den Blitz gezimmert Tvaschtar den himmlischen, der sch├╢nstes Werk vollendet, Mit dem er traf die Weichen auch des Vritra, mit raschem rasch der Herrscher vielen spendend.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬQuickly quaffing the libations, and devouring the grateful viands (presented) at the three (daily) sacrifices which are dedicated to the creator (of the world), he, the pervadere of the universe, stole the ripe (treasures of the asuras); the vanquisher (of his foes), the hurler of the thunderbolt, encountering pierced the cloud.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Viс╣гс╣Зu = pervader, an epithet applied to Indra, sarvasya jagato vy─Бpakaс╕е. Cloud = var─Бha. Viс╣гс╣Зu is the person nified yaj├▒a; he attracted the accusative ulated wealth of the asuras; then, he remained concealed behind seven difficult passes, or the days of initiatory preparation for the rite. Indra crossed the seven defiles or went through the seven days of initiation and pierced the sacrifice. Taittir─лya expands this further: Var─Бha, the stealer of what is beautiful, cherishes beyond the seven hills, the wealth of the asuras; Indra, having taken up the tufts of grass, and pierced the seven hills, slew him: var─Бhoyam vamamoс╣гaс╕е sapt─Бnam giriс╣З─Бm parast─Бd vittam vedyam asur─Бс╣З─Бm bibharti; sa darbhapi├▒julam uddhс╣Ыtya, sapta girin bhitv─Б, tam ahanniti

+Jamison Brereton

Just this oneтАФhe, having already drunk in an instant the nourishment of his great (father), the pleasing foods at his motherтАЩs
soma-pressingsтАФ
while Viс╣гс╣Зu the stronger stole the cooked (rice-porridge), he pierced the boar through the stone, (Indra) the archer.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On the introductory gen. asy├б referring to Indra, even though Indra is otherwise in the nominative in this verse (as subj. of papiv─Б╠Бn [b] and of v├нdhyat [d]), see disc. in introduction. and in Jamison 2007 noted above.

The verse concerns IndraтАЩs surreptitious drinking of his fatherтАЩs soma right after birth, an act enabled by his mother (ab), and Indra and Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs vanquishing of the Emuс╣гa boar (cd), a rarely told tale. For IndraтАЩs motherтАЩs complicity in the soma drinking, see esp. III.48.2-3. In our passage IndraтАЩs father is not directly referred to (only by initial mah├бс╕е тАШof the great [one]тАЩ in b), but the beginning of the next word promises the genitive of тАШfatherтАЩ (i.e., pit├║r), and only the final consonant of pit├║m removes that possibility тАФ one of the many tricks Nodhas plays on us in this hymn.

(Geldner ascribes the absence of pit├║с╕е to Worthaplologie, but I think rather that Nodhas is laying a trap.) On the basis of other tellings of the Emuс╣гa myth, the word to supply with pacat├бm is odan├бm тАШrice-porridgeтАЩ; cf. VIII.69.14, 77.6, 10.

The final p─Бda is quite artfully composed, beginning and ending with alliterative phrases: v├нdhyad var─Бh├бm and ├бdrim ├бst─Б. Moreover, the first of these is a variant of the very common formula that compresses the Vс╣Ыtra slaying, ├бhann ├бhim тАЬhe/you slew the serpent.тАЭ Here, with the victim beginning with v-, the poet substitutes a verb beginning with v-.

+Griffith

As soon as, at libations of his mother, great Visnu had drunk up the draught, he plundered.
The dainty cates, the cooked mess; but One stronger transfixed the wild boar, shooting through the mountain.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬTo that Indra the women, the wives of the gods, addressed their hymns, on the destruction of Ahi; he encompasses the extensive heaven and earth; they two do not surpass your vastness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Wives of the gods are person nified g─Бyatr─л and other metres of the Vedas; gn─Бс╕е, preceding devapatn─лс╕е means: feminine les whose nature is locomotive: gamanasvabh─Бvaс╕е

+Jamison Brereton

Just for this one, for Indra, even the ladies, the Wives of the Gods, wove a chant at the Vr╠еtra-smashing.
He held encircled broad heaven and earth; they did not encompass his greatness.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although I tr. dev├бpatn─лс╕е as тАШwives of the godsтАЩ, it is of course grammatically a bahuvr─лhi тАШhaving the gods as husbandsтАЩ (with the fem. stem patn─л- substituted for the masc. equivalent pati- in this feminine adjective). It reminds us of d─Бs├бpatn─л- тАШhaving a D─Бsa for a husbandтАЩ, applied to the waters confined by Vс╣Ыtra, often identified as a D─Бsa, most famously in I.32.11 but also twice elsewhere of the waters and Vс╣Ыtra (V.30.5, VIII.96.13). Since the context here is the Vс╣Ыtra battle (ahih├бtye), the complementary terminology is probably deliberate.

Jesse Lundquist notes that there is complementarity also in the second hemistich: 8c has p├бri jabhre with Indra as subject and dy─Б╠Бv─Бprthiv─л ╠Бas object, while 8d reverses this: n├б … p├бri staс╕е with dy─Б╠Бv─Бprthiv ╠е ─л ╠Бas implicit subj. and Indra as implicit object (via his mahim─Б╠Бnam). This theme and its lexicon are picked up in the 9ab: mahitv├бm / div├бs pс╣Ыthivy─Б╠Бс╕е p├бry ant├бrikс╣г─Бt.

+Griffith

To him, to Indra, when he slew the Dragon, the Dames, too, Consorts of the Gods, wove praises.
The mighty heaven and earth hath he encompassed: thy greatness heaven and earth, combined, exceed not.

+Geldner

Ihm, dem Indra, haben sogar die G├╢tterfrauen, die Gemahlinnen der G├╢tter im Drachenkampf ein Preislied erschallen lassen. Er h├дlt Himmel und Erde umfasst, die weiten; Nicht umschlie├Яen die beiden seine Gr├╢├Яe.

+Grassmann

Ihm woben auch die Fraun, die G├╢tterweiber dem Indra Loblied, als er schlug den Drachen, Er hat umfasst die weiten Erd’ und Himmel, nicht kommen gleich sie beide deiner Gr├╢sse.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHis magnitude verily exceeds that of the heaven, and earth and sky; Indra, self-irradiating in his dwelling, equal to every exploit, engaged with no unworthy foe, and killed in conflict, calls to battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Calling the clouds to battle or to collide, to genitive rate rain

+Jamison Brereton

Just this oneтАФhis greatness projected beyond heaven and earth, beyond the midspace.
Sovereign king, Indra, sung by all in the house, a reverberant tankard, waxed strong for battle [/for joy].

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The phrase тАЬreverberant tankardтАЭ (svar├нr ├бmatraс╕е) is striking, but intelligible in с╣Ъgvedic context. Indra is compared to a large drinking vessel because of his immense capacity and size, also described in 8cd and 9ab; тАЬtankardтАЭ hints at his ability to drink vast quantities of soma and implicitly promises his generosity because he can contain vast quantities of goods. I follow Oldenberg in taking all forms of ├бmatra- as belonging to a single stem (pace Grassmann, Lubotsky, and EWA). As for тАШreverberantтАЩ (svar├н-), it echoes svar─Б╠Бс╕╖, which opens the preceding p─Бda; it also suggests the deep sound made when a large (empty) vessel is struck and IndraтАЩs own war-cries. (For a possibly similar image, see I.100.12.)

+Griffith

Yea, of a truth, his magnitude surpasseth the magnitude of earth, mid-air, and heaven.
Indra, approved by all men, self-resplendent, waxed in his home, loud-voiced and strong for battle.

+Geldner

Seine Gr├╢├Яe reicht ├╝ber Himmel und Erde, ├╝ber das Luftreich hinaus. Indra ist der Selbstherrscher in seinem Hause, von allen gepriesen; ein nobler Herr, ein Gef├д├Я ist er zum Kampf herangewachsen.

+Grassmann

Es ├╝berragte wahrlich seine Gr├╢sse die weite Luft, den Himmel und die Erde; Selbstleuchtend wuchs im Hause allgepriesen der m├дcht’ge Indra tobend auf zum Kampfe.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThrough his power, the rivers sport, since he has opened (a way for them) by his thunderbolt; establishing his supremacy and granting a (recompense) to the giver (of the oblation), he, the swift-moving provided a resting plural ce for T┼лrv─лti.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

T┼лrv─лti is a с╣Ыс╣гi who had been immersed in water; Indra brought him to dry land

+Jamison Brereton

Just this oneтАФthe rivers with their glittering came to rest when he held them encircled with his mace.
Performing the masterтАЩs part, showing favor to the pious man, the victorious one made a ford for Turv─лti.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse nicely juxtaposes a well-known deed of IndraтАЩs, when he stops the waters to make a ford for his client(s), with the even better known deed of releasing the stopped waters in the Vс╣Ыtra myth, treated in the preceding vs. (10). On the playful transition between these two myths here, see Jamison 2007: 113-14 n. 20. The stopping of the waters causes mild surprise immediately after a verse concerning their release.

tveс╣г├бs─Б is universally taken as belonging to Indra, whereas my published translation

ascribes it to the rivers. I would now probably correct this, also to take it as IndraтАЩs: тАЬjust this one - with his turbulence/glittering,тАЭ because of the parallelism between 10a asy├йd ev├б ┼Ы├бvas─Б and 11a asy├йd u tveс╣г├б┼Ы─Б. But I am still disturbed by the form.

Its accent suggests that it should be adjectival, not a neuter -s-stem abstract like ┼Ы├бvas-, despite AiG II.2.224, which implies that it is nominal despite its accent. It is curious that the expected root-accented neut. noun (*tv├йс╣гas-) is not attested, and this is the only (supposed) attestation of the suffix-accented stem. If it is a real adjective, it could modify v├бjreс╣Зa in p─Бda b, but this not only breaks the parallelism between 10a and 11a just noted, but, more seriously, would have to be extracted from one clause and plunked into the next. (Geldner in his note suggests supplying v├бjreс╣Зa in p─Бda a.) The a-stem adj. tveс╣г├б- is also sometimes used of waters, e.g., VI.61.8 tveс╣г├бс╕е тАж arс╣Зav├бс╕е тАЬglittering/turbulent flood,тАЭ which accounts for my original connection of tveс╣г├бs─Б with the rivers.

The distribution of elements in p─Бda b is odd, with the subordinating y├бd in normal 2nd position, but s─лm, ordinarily another 2nd position element, just before the verb.

─л┼Ы─Бna-kс╣Ы╠Бt- is variously interpreted, either with the 1st member in a direct object relationship with the 2nd – тАЬzum Herrscher, m├дchtig machendтАЭ (ScarlattaтАЩs tr; sim.

also Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) - or in a sort of appositive subject relationship, тАЬals Herrscher handelndтАЭ (ScarlattaтАЩs tr.; sim. Grassmann). Because the first member ─л┼Ы─Бna- is itself a participial form тАШbeing lord, showing masteryтАЩ, I prefer the 2nd alternative. Note also that independent ─л╠Б┼Ы─Бna- is used three times of Indra in this hymn (6d, 12b, 15b), and it is more likely that the same form in the compound refers to IndraтАЩs masterful ways, not to someone else whom he makes masterful. Scarlatta allows both, though somewhat preferring the 2nd.

More phonological play: c d─Б┼Ы├║с╣гe da┼Ыasyan; d turv─л╠Бtaye тАж turv├бс╣Зiс╕е.

+Griffith

The rivers played, through his impetuous splendour, since with his bolt he compassed them on all sides.
Using his might and favouring him who worshipped, he made a ford, victorious, for Turviti.

+Geldner

Durch seinen Feuereifer standen die Str├╢me still, als er sie mit der Keule zur├╝ckhielt. Reich machend, dem Opferwilligen gef├дllig, bereite der Erretter dem Turviti eine Furt.

+Grassmann

Auf seinen Antrieb rannen hin die Str├╢me, als er auf Vritra mit dem Blitz gezielet, Der Herrscher, Gunst dem Huldiger erweisend, macht’ freie Bahn als Sieger dem Turviti.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, who are the quick moving and strength-endowed lord (of all), hurl your thunderbolt against this Vс╣Ыtra and sever his joints, as (butchers cut up) a cow, that the rains may issue from him, and the waters flow (over the earth).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The text says, ‘cut in pieces the limbs of Vс╣Ыtra, as of a cow’ (gorna);

Added: ‘as worldly men, the carvers (vikarat─Бraс╕е) of flesh, divide here and there the limbs of animals

+Jamison Brereton

Toward just this one, toward Vr╠еtra, bear down the mace, thrusting, gaining mastery, conferring (who knows) how much.
Scrape through him crosswise as if through the joints of a cow, dispatching the floods of waters to wander.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On this very tricky verse, I simply reproduce (slightly paraphrased) my discussion of it in Jamison 2007: 66: The beginning of 12 appears to return us from the mythological past to the realm of the current-day poet of vss. 1-5; not only does it start with the dative pronoun after a series of verses with the genitive phrase but it continues with a standard lexeme for presenting a hymn to a divinity: pr├б тИЪbhr╠е: asm─Б╠Б├нd u pr├б bhar─Б … Cf. from the same poet also with a dative recipient I.64.1b.

n├│dhaс╕е suvrkt ╠е ├нm pr├б bhar─Б mar├║dbhyaс╕е тАЬO Nodhas, present a well-turned (hymn) to the Maruts.тАЭ But the phrase in 61.12 quickly goes awry. At the opening of the next p─Бda, where Indra’s name has been prominently placed in previous verses (├нndr─Бya 1d, 4d, 5b, 8b), we find, most shockingly, the name of his arch-enemy, vr╠еtr─Б╠Бya, immediately followed by the accusative object v├бjram, Indra’s weapon, not the word for hymn we were expecting. The relevant parts of the half-verse asm─Б╠Б├нd u pr├б bhar─Б…, vrtr╠е ─Б╠Бya v├бjram… must mean “Towards just this one, towards Vr╠еtra, bear down the mace…” The poet has simply tricked us, having laid a trap with conventional phraseology and syntax and with the stylistic patterns established earlier in the hymn. He also skillfully exploits the morphological ambiguity of the verb form bhar─Б: given the pattern set in vss. 1-5 we are primed to interpret bhar─Б as a 1st sg. subjunctive (cf. indicative bh├бr─Бmi in vss 2-3), but as the half verse unfolds, it becomes clear that bhar─Б must rather be taken as a metrically lengthened 2nd sg.

imperative. [end of citation] In order to let the audience in on the trick, the poet has imported much of verse 6, the first mention of the Vс╣Ыtra conflict in this hymn: 6d reads tuj├бnn ─л╠Б┼Ы─Бnas tujat─Б╠Бkiydh─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬgaining mastery, thrusting with the thrusting (mace), while conferring (who knows) how much,тАЭ while 12ab echoes this with тАж t┼л╠Бtuj─Бno, тАж ─л╠Б┼Ы─Бnaс╕е kiyedh─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬthrusting, gaining mastery, conferring (who knows) how much.тАЭ In d ├нс╣гyan echoes ─л╠Б┼Ы─Бnaс╕е of p─Бda b (as well as 11c) and anticipates iс╣гс╣З─Бn├бс╕е of 13c.

+Griffith

Vast, with thine ample power, with eager movement, against this Vrtra cast thy bolt of thunder.
Rend thou his joints, as of an ox, dissevered, with bolt oblique, that floods of rain may follow.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬProclaim, with new hymns, the former exploits of that quick-moving Indra, when wielding his weapons in battle, he encounters and destroys his enemies.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Of just this one, the precipitousтАФproclaim his former deeds anew with solemn words,
when, propelling his own weapons to battle, showing his mettle, he dissolves his rivals.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On this verse as a species of тАЬpoetic repairтАЭ of verse 12, see Jamison 2007: 66-67. The expected offering of praise to Indra thwarted in 12ab is successfully effected in 13ab.

+Griffith

Sing with new lauds his exploits wrought aforetime, the deeds of him, yea, him who moveth swiftly,
When, hurling forth his weapons in the battle, he with impetuous wrath lays low the foemen.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

Des starken Indra alte Heldenthaten verk├╝nde nun aufs neue durch Ges├дnge, Wie er zum Kampfe seine Waffen schwingend, im Zorne bebend niederwirft die Feinde.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThrough fear of him, the stable mountains (are still), and through dread of his appearance, heaven and earth tremble; may, Nodhas, praising repeatedly the preserving power of that beloved Indra, be speedily (blessed) with vigour.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Just this oneтАФin fear of his birth both the firmly fixed mountains and heaven and earth thrust against each.
Constantly calling upon him [=Indra], who is a (protective) arm for the seeker, in an instant Nodhas [=the poet] will be (there) for his
[=IndraтАЩs] (next?) manly deed.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

dy─Б╠Бv─Б ca bh┼л╠Бm─Б has the appearance of a dual dvandva, interrupted by the ca that connects it to the NP with which itтАЩs conjoined, gir├бya┼Ы ca dс╣Ыс╕╖h─Б╠Бс╕е. But the uninterrupted dvandva is actually dy─Б╠Бv─Бbh┼л╠Бm─л, with a different stem for тАШearthтАЩ, and bh┼л╠Бman- (n.) has no dual attested (and its dual should of course not be bh┼л╠Бm─Б, but probably *bh┼лman─л). See the next hymn for a variant on this usage. It is likely that the lengthened N/A sg. form or the N/A pl. form is being used, but why? On this problem, see AiG II.1.152.

In the published translation, тАЬotherтАЭ was careless omitted at the end of the first hemistich: it should read тАЬagainst each other.тАЭ The mention of the poet Nodhas at the very end of the verse has perhaps been prepared by several not entirely expected oтАЩs: ├║po … j├│guv─Бna oс╣З├нс╣Г, sady├│, only the last of which is a normal sandhi o тЖР -as. The poetтАЩs fondness for his own vowel may account for the appearance of several relatively rare words: the intensive j├│gu- and the noun oс╣З├н-.

+Griffith

When he, yea, he, comes forth the firm. Set mountains and the whole heaven and earth, tremble for terror.
May Nodhas, ever praising the protection of that dear Friend, gain quickly strength heroic.

+Geldner

Aus Furcht vor seiner Geburt fahren sowohl die festen Berge wie Himmel und Erde erschrocken zusammen. Ihn Anrufend, der f├╝r den Seher ein sch├╝tzender Arm ist, m├╢ge Nodhas alsbald seiner Mannestat gew├дrtig sein.

+Grassmann

Die festen Berge, ja auch Erd’ und Himmel bewegen sich aus Furcht vor dem gebornen, Verk├╝ndend laut die H├╝lfe nun des holden, m├╢g’ Nodhas schnell zu Heldenkraft gelangen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬTo him has that praise been offered which he, sole (victor over his foes), and lord of maniford wealth, prefers (to receive) from those (who praise him). Indra has defended the pious sacrificer Eta┼Ыa when contending with S┼лrya, the son of Sva┼Ыva.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Legend: A king names Sva┼Ыva (lord of good horses, su a┼Ыva) was desirous of a son; he worshipped S┼лrya, who was also born as the son of a king. There was a dispute between him and с╣Ыс╣гi Eta┼Ыa. Indra sided with the latter

+Jamison Brereton

Just to this one has this (soma-drinking?) been conceded by them [=gods], since he alone won (it?), becoming master of much.
Indra aided Eta┼Ыa, who was contending for the sun; he will aid the
soma-presser contending for good horses.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow GeldnerтАЩs suggestion (in n. to 15a, followed by Witzel Got┼Н) that the unexpressed subject that is being conceded to Indra is the soma-drink. The parallel he adduces, V.29.5, contains the gods, the soma-drink, the concession, and Eta┼Ыa: ├бdha kr├бtv─Б maghavan t├║bhyaс╣Г dev─Б╠Б├бnu v├н┼Ыve adaduс╕е somap├йyam y├бt s┼л╠Бryasya har├нtaс╕е p├бtant─лс╕е pur├бс╕е sat─л╠Бr ├║par─Б ├йta┼Ыe k├бс╕е Then according to your will, o bounteous one, all the gods conceded the soma-drinking to you, when you put the flying golden mares of the Sun behind, though they were in front, in Eta┼Ыa(’s presence).

In the published translation I take eс╣г─Бm as a genitival agent, somewhat reluctantly. However, Elizabeth Tucker suggests a much more attractive solution, which rescues the syntax: that eс╣г─Б╠Бm is dependent on asma├н тАЬjust to this one of them [=gods].тАЭ The singularity of Indra would then be emphasized by the ├йkaс╕е that begins the next p─Бda.

Eta┼Ыa is the horse of the Sun and is not, as far as I know, a soma-presser (the physical image is a little comical). Against all tr., I therefore do not take s├║с╣гvim in d as coreferential with ├йta┼Ыam in c, but rather as a second object with the verb. Nodhas is now juggling the mythic past (the aiding of Eta┼Ыa) and the desired future (the aiding of the soma-presser), as he nears the end of the hymn. I read the participle paspс╣Ыdh─Бn├бm twice, once with each object, with a different desired goal in the locative for each. I also give the verb ─Бvat two simultaneous morphological analyses, fitting its two objects: the first as augmented imperfect to the Class I present ├бvati, the second as perfect subjunctive to the pf. ─Б╠Бva (cf. ─Бpas, ─Бpat taken by Hoffmann 1967: 64 n. 102, 101 n. 220, and K├╝mmel 2000: 118 as subjunctives to pf. ─Б╠Бpa тИЪ─Бp тАШattainтАЩ). Although such an interpretation might be too artificial in some cases, I have no hesitation in assuming Nodhas is capable of this.

Another phonetic play: d sa├║va┼Ыvi ye s├║с╣гvim

+Griffith

Now unto him of these things hath been given what he who rules alone o’er much, electeth.
Indra hath helped Etasa, Soma-presser, contending in the race of steeds with Surya.

+Geldner

Ihm Ward das von ihnen zugestanden, was er allein errungen hat, der ├╝ber vieles Macht hat. Dem um den Surya k├дmpfenden Etasa, dem Somaopferer, stand Indra bei im Wettstreit um die besten Rosse.

+Grassmann

So ist ihm das von G├╢ttern zugestanden, was er begehrt, der eine viel besitzend, Er half dem Ross im Wettlauf mit der Sonne, dem Frommen half zu hohem Gl├╝cke Indra.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIndra, harnesser of steeds, the descendants of Gotama have offered to you prayers of efficacy to secure your presence; bestow upon them every sort of affluence; may he who has acquired wealth by pious acts, come hither quickly in the morning.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Thus have the Gotamas made you sacred formulations for the
тАЬFallow-bay-yokingтАЭ (oblation), with a good twist, o Indra.
Do you confer on them an insight with all its ornaments. тАУ Early in the morningтАФsoonтАФhe should come bringing goods through his
insight.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

h─Бriyojan─Б is unaccented and therefore taken by most as a vocative addressed to Indra. I follow Oldenberg in emending to an accented form (h─Бriyojan─Б╠Б), modifying br├бhm─Бс╣Зi. See in the next hymn br├бhma hariy├│jan─Бya тАЬformulation for the fallow-bay-yoking.тАЭ As Oldenberg points out, taking it as a vocative with Indra requires either shortening the last vowel or allowing a lengthened vocative ending (which is not usual), and possibly also shortening the first vowel.

This verse is extra-hymnic in some ways: its opening breaks the pattern set in the previous 15 vss.; it makes a meta-announcement about the contents of the hymn just recited; and it ends with the Nodhas refrain. But it also forms a ring with the first verse, with the repetition of br├бhm─Бс╣Зi, and with the first part of the hymn concerning the presentation of praise-hymns, with the reappearance of suvс╣Ыkt├н, which was a signature word there (2b, 3d, 4c).

+Griffith

Thus to thee, Indra, yoker of Bay Coursers, the Gotamas have brought their prayers to please thee.
Bestow upon them thought, decked with all beauty. May he, enriched with prayer, come soon and early.

+Geldner

So haben dir, du Trinker des Falbenanschirrungsschoppens, mit sch├╢ner Lobrede die Gotamiden eine Erbauung bereitet, o Indra. Leg in sie die Dichtung mit allen Zierden! - Recht bald am Morgen soll sich der einstellen, der durch die Weisheit Sch├дtze erwirbt.

+Grassmann

So haben preisend dir, der F├╝chse anschirrt, die Gotamer Gebet verrichtet, Indra, Lass reich mit Gut geschm├╝ckt sein ihre Andacht. Der huldvoll sorget, komme fr├╝h am Morgen.

+Elizarenkova
